Summary of Depth Estimation Results:

1. Mean Absolute Error (MAE):

   - MAE represents the average error between the predicted depth and the actual depth.

   - HITNET MAE: 0.6112

   - CRE MAE: 0.6291

   - D455 MAE: 0.6076

   The lower the MAE, the better the model is at estimating depth accurately.


2. Root Mean Squared Error (RMSE):

   - RMSE is similar to MAE but gives more weight to larger errors.

   - HITNET RMSE: 1.5743

   - CRE RMSE: 1.5942

   - D455 RMSE: 1.5505

   Lower RMSE values indicate fewer large discrepancies in depth estimation.


3. Mean Squared Error (MSE):

   - MSE is similar to RMSE but doesn't convert back to original units.

   - HITNET MSE: 4.3722

   - CRE MSE: 4.4536

   - D455 MSE: 4.1766

   Like RMSE, lower MSE values indicate better performance.


4. Intersection over Union (IoU):

   - IoU measures how well the predicted depth overlaps with the ground truth.

   - HITNET IoU: 0.7670

   - CRE IoU: 0.7694

   - D455 IoU: 0.6852

   Higher IoU values indicate better spatial agreement between the prediction and ground truth.


6. Percentage of Erroneous Pixels (D1):

   - D1 calculates the percentage of pixels where the disparity error exceeds a threshold (e.g., 3 pixels).

   - HITNET D1: 3.85%

   - CRE D1: 3.93%

   - D455 D1: 3.55%

   A lower D1 percentage means fewer significant errors, indicating a more reliable depth estimation model, especially in real-world scenarios where accuracy is crucial.


Conclusion:

   - D455 had the best overall performance in terms of average accuracy (lowest MAE).

   - D455 was the most consistent, with the lowest squared errors (lowest RMSE).

   - D455 minimized large errors the most (lowest MSE).

   - CRE had the best spatial overlap with the ground truth (highest IoU).

   - D455 had the fewest significant errors (lowest D1 percentage).
